### Bash - 2026-03-07 13:06:41 UTC [14:06:41 CEST]

**User Request:** <objective>
Extract implementation decisions that downstream agents need — researcher and planner will use CONTEXT.md to know what to investigate and what choices are locked.

**How it works:**
1. Load prior context (PROJECT.md, REQUIREMENTS.md, STATE.md, prior CONTEXT.md files)
2. Scout codebase for reusable assets and patterns
3. Analyze phase — skip gray areas already decided in prior phases
4. Present remaining gray areas — user selects which to discuss
5. Deep-dive each selected area until satisfied
6. Create CONTEXT.md with decisions that guide research and planning

**Output:** `{phase_num}-CONTEXT.md` — decisions clear enough that downstream agents can act without asking the user again
</objective>

<execution_context>
@/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/.claude/get-shit-done/workflows/discuss-phase.md
@/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/.claude/get-shit-done/templates/context.md
</execution_context>

<context>
Phase number: 10 (required)

Context files are resolved in-workflow using `init phase-op` and roadmap/state tool calls.
</context>

<process>
1. Validate phase number (error if missing or not in roadmap)
2. Check if CONTEXT.md exists (offer update/view/skip if yes)
3. **Load prior context** — Read PROJECT.md, REQUIREMENTS.md, STATE.md, and all prior CONTEXT.md files
4. **Scout codebase** — Find reusable assets, patterns, and integration points
5. **Analyze phase** — Check prior decisions, skip already-decided areas, generate remaining gray areas
6. **Present gray areas** — Multi-select: which to discuss? Annotate with prior decisions + code context
7. **Deep-dive each area** — 4 questions per area, code-informed options, Context7 for library choices
8. **Write CONTEXT.md** — Sections match areas discussed + code_context section
9. Offer next steps (research or plan)

**CRITICAL: Scope guardrail**
- Phase boundary from ROADMAP.md is FIXED
- Discussion clarifies HOW to implement, not WHETHER to add more
- If user suggests new capabilities: "That's its own phase. I'll note it for later."
- Capture deferred ideas — don't lose them, don't act on them

**Domain-aware gray areas:**
Gray areas depend on what's being built. Analyze the phase goal:
- Something users SEE → layout, density, interactions, states
- Something users CALL → responses, errors, auth, versioning
- Something users RUN → output format, flags, modes, error handling
- Something users READ → structure, tone, depth, flow
- Something being ORGANIZED → criteria, grouping, naming, exceptions

Generate 3-4 **phase-specific** gray areas, not generic categories.

**Probing depth:**
- Ask 4 questions per area before checking
- "More questions about [area], or move to next?"
- If more → ask 4 more, check again
- After all areas → "Ready to create context?"

**Do NOT ask about (Claude handles these):**
- Technical implementation
- Architecture choices
- Performance concerns
- Scope expansion
</process>

<success_criteria>
- Prior context loaded and applied (no re-asking decided questions)
- Gray areas identified through intelligent analysis
- User chose which areas to discuss
- Each selected area explored until satisfied
- Scope creep redirected to deferred ideas
- CONTEXT.md captures decisions, not vague vision
- User knows next steps
</success_criteria>

**Tool:** Bash
**Input:** ```json
{
  "command": "INIT=$(node \"$HOME/.claude/get-shit-done/bin/gsd-tools.cjs\" init phase-op \"10\") && if [[ \"$INIT\" == @file:* ]]; then INIT=$(cat \"${INIT#@file:}\"); fi && echo \"$INIT\"",
  "description": "Initialize phase-op for phase 10"
}
```

**Result:** ✅ Success
**Output:** ```
{
  "commit_docs": true,
  "brave_search": false,
  "phase_found": true,

  "phase_number": "10",
  "phase_name": "kg-operations-restoration",
  "phase_slug": "kg-operations-restoration",

**Domain-aware gray areas:**

- Something users SEE → layout, density, interactions, states
- Something users CALL → responses, errors, auth, versioning
- Something users RUN → output format, flags, modes, error handling
- Something users READ → structure, tone, depth, flow
- Something being ORGANIZED → criteria, grouping, naming, exceptions

Generate 3-4 **phase-specific** gray areas, not generic categories.

**Probing depth:**
- Ask 4 questions per area before checking
- "More questions about [area], or move to next?"
- If more → ask 4 more, check again
- After all areas → "Ready to create context?"

- Architecture choices

- Scope expansion

        },

        },

1. Load prior context (PROJECT.md, REQUIREMENTS.md, STATE.md, prior CONTEXT.md files)
2. Scout codebase for reusable assets and patterns
3. Analyze phase — skip gray areas already decided in prior phases
4. Present remaining gray areas — user selects which to discuss
5. Deep-dive each selected area until satisfied
6. Create CONTEXT.md with decisions that guide research and planning

</objective>

<process>
1. Validate phase number (error if missing or not in roadmap)
2. Check if CONTEXT.md exists (offer update/view/skip if yes)
3. **Load prior context** — Read PROJECT.md, REQUIREMENTS.md, STATE.md, and all prior CONTEXT.md files
4. **Scout codebase** — Find reusable assets, patterns, and integration points
5. **Analyze phase** — Check prior decisions, skip already-decided areas, generate remaining gray areas
6. **Present gray areas** — Multi-select: which to discuss? Annotate with prior decisions + code context
7. **Deep-dive each area** — 4 questions per area, code-informed options, Context7 for library choices
8. **Write CONTEXT.md** — Sections match areas discussed + code_context section
9. Offer next steps (research or plan)

**CRITICAL: Scope guardrail**
- Phase boundary from ROADMAP.md is FIXED
- Discussion clarifies HOW to implement, not WHETHER to add more
- If user suggests new capabilities: "That's its own phase. I'll note it for later."
- Capture deferred ideas — don't lose them, don't act on them

**Domain-aware gray areas:**
Gray areas depend on what's being built. Analyze the phase goal:
- Something users SEE → layout, density, interactions, states
- Something users CALL → responses, errors, auth, versioning
- Something users RUN → output format, flags, modes, error handling
- Something users READ → structure, tone, depth, flow
- Something being ORGANIZED → criteria, grouping, naming, exceptions

Generate 3-4 **phase-specific** gray areas, not generic categories.

**Probing depth:**
- Ask 4 questions per area before checking
- "More questions about [area], or move to next?"
- If more → ask 4 more, check again
- After all areas → "Ready to create context?"

**Do NOT ask about (Claude handles these):**
- Technical implementation
- Architecture choices
- Performance concerns
- Scope expansion
</process>

- Gray areas identified through intelligent analysis
- User chose which areas to discuss
- Each selected area explored until satisfied
- Scope creep redirected to deferred ideas
- CONTEXT.md captures decisions, not vague vision
- User knows next steps
</success_criteria>

**Input:** ```json
{
  "questions": [
    {
      "question": "generateEmbedding() currently returns random 384-dim vectors (mock). For real semantic similarity in dedup/pred operators, you need actual embeddings. What approach?",
      "header": "Embeddings",
      "options": [
        {
          "label": "LLM-based embeddings",
          "description": "Use the existing LLM provider (Anthropic/OpenAI) embedding endpoint. Real semantic similarity. Adds API calls and cost per entity. OpenAI text-embedding-3-small is cheap and fast."
        },
        {
          "label": "Local sentence-transformers",
          "description": "Run sentence-transformers in the Docker container (Python). No API cost, fast inference. Requires adding Python + model to Docker image (~500MB). numpy/sentence-transformers already partially present."
        },
        {
          "label": "Keep mock, flag for later",
          "description": "Ship with mock embeddings + a flag. Operators run but embed/pred produce random results. Focus on getting operator pipeline wired correctly first, swap in real embeddings later."
        },
        {
          "label": "You decide",
          "description": "Claude picks based on Docker constraints and operator usefulness"
        }
      ],
      "multiSelect": false
    }
  ]
}
```

        {
          "label": "Cross-wave accumulation (Recommended)",

        },
        {

        },
        {
          "label": "Empty accumulated KG",
          "description": "Since it's full-replace-per-run, there IS no accumulated KG. Operators run on the current run's entities only. Dedup catches duplicates within this run, pred predicts edges within this run's entities."
        },
        {
          "label": "You decide",

        }
      ],
      "multiSelect": false
    }
  ]

This phase restores the 6 KG operators (conv, aggr, embed, dedup, pred, merge) into the wave pipeline. It does not add content validation/QA (Phase 11) or trace display UI (Phase 12).\n\n</domain>\n\n<decisions>\n## Implementation Decisions\n\n### Operator placement\n- All 6 operators run post-pipeline: AFTER all 3 waves complete but BEFORE insight finalization (Wave 4)\n- Operators get the full entity set from all waves, enabling cross-hierarchy dedup/merge/pred\n- All 6 operators enabled: conv adapts to wave mode using run metadata instead of batch dates\n- Each operator gets its own dashboard progress step (operator_conv, operator_aggr, etc.) matching old pipeline behavior\n- Operator failures are graceful: each operator wrapped in try/catch, failure logs warning and skips that operator, pipeline continues\n- Use KGOperators.applyAll() to sequence operators internally -- less code in wave-controller\n\n### Embedding strategy\n- Local sentence-transformers via Python subprocess (NOT mock, NOT LLM API)\n- Model: all-MiniLM-L6-v2 (384-dim, ~80MB) -- matches existing mock dimension\n- Downloaded at Docker build time (baked into image, no lazy download)\n- Batch all entities in one subprocess call -- sentence-transformers handles internal batching\n- Embeddings persisted on entities in the knowledge graph (stored on KGEntity.embedding)\n- Embedding subprocess fallback: Claude's discretion (graceful skip of embed + pred operators, or TF-IDF fallback)\n\n### Dedup scope and behavior\n- Hierarchy-aware dedup: dedup key includes parentId, same-name entities under different parents are NOT merged\n- Two-pass dedup: first pass is exact normalized name match, second pass uses embedding cosine similarity\n- Semantic dedup auto-merges above threshold (cosine > 0.9 AND same hierarchy level AND same parent)\n- mergeEntities() parentId fix (KGOP-06): incoming hierarchy fields win -- `parentId: incoming.parentId ?? existing.parentId`, same for level and hierarchyPath\n\n### Accumulated KG and operator context\n- Cross-wave accumulation: all 3 waves' entities form the complete set for post-pipeline operators\n- Since operators run post-pipeline on the full set, accumulated KG = the entities produced by all waves in this run\n- Edge prediction (pred): cross-branch only -- compare entities in different L1 branches, skip same-branch pairs (they already have explicit parent-child relations)\n- Conv context: build BatchContext from run metadata (run timestamp, recent git commits from repo, session count) -- adapts to wave mode without changing conv interface\n\n### Claude's Discretion\n- Embedding subprocess fallback strategy (skip embed+pred or TF-IDF)\n- Exact cosine similarity threshold for semantic dedup (starting point: 0.9)\n- How to collect recent git commits and sessions for conv's BatchContext\n- Dashboard progress integration details for individual operator steps\n- Whether applyAll() needs modification to emit per-operator progress events or if wave-controller wraps it\n\n</decisions>\n\n<code_context>\n## Existing Code Insights\n\n### Reusable Assets\n- `KGOperators` class (kg-operators.ts:96): Full 6-operator pipeline with applyAll(). Already has conv, aggr, embed, dedup, pred, merge methods\n- `createKGOperators()` (kg-operators.ts:679): Factory function taking SemanticAnalyzer\n- `mergeEntities()` (kg-operators.ts:400): Merge logic -- needs parentId null-coalesce fix\n- `generateEmbedding()` (semantic-analyzer.ts:721): Currently mock (random 384-dim) -- replace with real sentence-transformers call\n- `embedding_generator.py` (src/utils/): Partial Python embedding script -- needs numpy + sentence-transformers installed\n- Old coordinator pipeline (coordinator.ts:3327-3422): Individual operator step progression with progress tracking -- reference for dashboard integration\n\n### Established Patterns\n- Wave persistence via PersistenceAgent (wave-controller.ts:463) -- operators run after this\n- Individual progress steps per operator in old pipeline (coordinator.ts:285) -- same pattern for wave pipeline\n- Graceful fallback with flags (Phase 9: shallow_analysis flag on SemanticAnalysisAgent failure)\n- Full replace per run (Phase 7 decision) -- entities replaced each run, manifest accumulates\n- Per-entity atomic pipeline in waves (Phase 9) -- operators run on the accumulated result post-waves\n\n### Integration Points\n- `wave-controller.ts`: Add operator phase between wave 3 persistence and insight finalization (Wave 4)\n- `kg-operators.ts`: Fix mergeEntities() hierarchy fields, update dedup to be hierarchy-aware, adapt conv for run metadata\n- `semantic-analyzer.ts`: Replace mock generateEmbedding() with real sentence-transformers subprocess call\n- `Dockerfile`: Add numpy + sentence-transformers + all-MiniLM-L6-v2 model download to build stage\n- Dashboard progress: operator steps need to be registered in the progress tracking system\n\n</code_context>\n\n<specifics>\n## Specific Ideas\n\n- Operators run as a distinct phase between wave completion and insight finalization -- \"Wave 4\" becomes \"Wave 5\" or insight finalization stays Wave 4 but operators are a named step between waves and insights\n- Cross-branch edge prediction discovers relationships like \"ErrorHandler relates_to Logger\" across different component branches -- the kind of insight that wave-per-branch analysis misses\n- Semantic dedup with real embeddings can catch near-duplicates the wave agents create independently (e.g., two wave 3 agents both creating a \"ConfigurationManagement\" detail under different parents)\n\n</specifics>\n\n<deferred>\n## Deferred Ideas\n\nNone -- discussion stayed within phase
